    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }

      AppleID.auth.init({

      <div id="description" class="readable stacked" style="right:0">
        
<span id="freeTextContainer11071459196038383253">Part Eternal Sunshine of the Spotless Mind, part Aristotle and Dante Discover the Secrets of the Universe, Adam Silvera's extraordinary debut confronts race, class, and sexuality during one charged near-future summer in the Bronx. <br/><br/>Sixteen-year-old Aaron Soto is struggling to find happiness after a family tragedy leaves him reeling. He's slowly remembering what happiness mi</span>
  <span id="freeText11071459196038383253" style="display:none">Part Eternal Sunshine of the Spotless Mind, part Aristotle and Dante Discover the Secrets of the Universe, Adam Silvera's extraordinary debut confronts race, class, and sexuality during one charged near-future summer in the Bronx. <br /><br />Sixteen-year-old Aaron Soto is struggling to find happiness after a family tragedy leaves him reeling. He's slowly remembering what happiness might feel like this summer with the support of his girlfriend Genevieve, but it's his new best friend, Thomas, who really gets Aaron to open up about his past and confront his future.<br /><br />As Thomas and Aaron get closer, Aaron discovers things about himself that threaten to shatter his newfound contentment. A revolutionary memory-alteration procedure, courtesy of the Leteo Institute, might be the way to straighten himself out. But what if it means forgetting who he truly is?</span>
  <a data-text-id="11071459196038383253" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

      </div>
</div>

<div class='questionText'>
<a href="/questions/365351-is-this-book-appropriate-for-14-year-olds">is this book appropriate for 14 year olds?</a>
</div>
<div class='communityQAFooter questionFooter'>
<ul class='questionFooterActions'>
<li class='footerItem like'>
<span class='likeItContainer' id='like_container_community_question_365351'><a id="like_count_community_question_365351" rel="nofollow" href="/rating/voters/365351?resource_type=CommunityQuestion"><span class="likesCount">5 likes</span></a>&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;<a rel="nofollow" class="jsLike like_it" href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/new?remember=true&amp;return_url=%2Fbook%2Fshow%2F19542841-more-happy-than-not">like</a></span>

</li>
<li class='footerItem communityQuestionTimestamp'>
<a href="/questions/365351-is-this-book-appropriate-for-14-year-olds">5 years ago</a>
</li>
<li class='footerItem communityQuestionPermalink'>
<a href="/questions/365351-is-this-book-appropriate-for-14-year-olds">See all 14 answers</a>

<div class='allCommunityAnswers'>
<div class='communityAnswer'>
<div class='communityAnswerBody'>
<div class='answererUserIcon'>
<a class="leftAlignedImage userPhoto" href="/user/show/9992398-cat"><img alt="" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/users/1472933653i/9992398._UY100_CR1,0,100,100_.jpg" /></a>
</div>
<div class='communityAnswerTextContainer'>
<span class='communityAnswererName'>
<a href="/user/show/9992398-cat">Cat</a>
</span>
<span class='communityAnswerText'>
<span class="expandableContainer"><span class="truncatedContent">I would say yes, but I'm a firm believer that kids should be exposed to difficult and complex topics because that's life - encountering it first in fi<a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">I would say yes, but I'm a firm believer that kids should be exposed to difficult and complex topics because that's life - encountering it first in fiction makes things less frightening when experienced first hand. It's a coming of age story, so there are sexual awakenings and characters figuring out who they are and what friendships/romantic relationships mean. On top of that there are themes of loss, grief, and depression. <br /><br />In some ways it's a pretty heavy book, but it's also accessible for young readers - it would get the message across that not everyone has a squeaky clean life, and that's ok. Some 14 year olds will be more ready and receptive to this than others, but I'm always hesitant to say someone is too young because the topics are complex. People are gay, people are depressed, people swear, people have sex, sex is confusing, and puberty is the wooooooorst - kids know all this already, but if it's normalized early on then maybe it won't be so hard for them to talk about it as they're going through it.<a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>
</span>
</div>
</div>

        $$('span.elementTwo').each(function (e) {
          if (e.getStyle('display') !== 'none') {
            var lessLink = e.next();
            swapContent(lessLink);
          }
        });
      });

//]]>
</script>    </div>

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14596170-cristina-monica?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1204409916" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14087818012832010630"><b>POWERFUL. POIGNANT. INDISPENSABLE BOOK. </b><br/><br/>Oh, damn, what a rollercoaster of emotions this was. Havoc in my heart. I wish I could say that it made me smile or laugh or dream, but that would be lying to you and myself. It is very unlikely that you will turn the last page and sigh, hand on your heart and stars in your eyes. You will very likely be clutching at your heart, in fear that it will break. In hindsight, I realize that I had no idea what I was getting into. When I heard people qualifying thi</span>
  <span id="freeText14087818012832010630" style="display:none"><b>POWERFUL. POIGNANT. INDISPENSABLE BOOK. </b><br><br>Oh, damn, what a rollercoaster of emotions this was. Havoc in my heart. I wish I could say that it made me smile or laugh or dream, but that would be lying to you and myself. It is very unlikely that you will turn the last page and sigh, hand on your heart and stars in your eyes. You will very likely be clutching at your heart, in fear that it will break. In hindsight, I realize that I had no idea what I was getting into. When I heard people qualifying this book as ‘‘sad’’ and ‘‘gut-wrenching’’, I thought that they were straight out exaggerating. <br><br>They weren’t. <br><br>But while I wish I could make a camp fire out of this book and watch it distort itself into nothingness, I’m also glad that I read it. Homophobia still exists. Suicides still happen. Hearts still break. I don’t know anyone who would willingly dive into a book and hope for it to shatter them. I do, however, know that those themes are ones that undoubtedly hurt but are important, because they’re sadly part of this world and the more we read about them, the more we understand what they are, what they mean. And knowledge is everything, isn’t that right?<br><br>I won’t say that this book is beautiful or wonderful, but I will admit that it is <u>unforgettable</u>. I can’t imagine someone finishing it and just carrying on with their lives, letting oblivion steal every thought concerning MORE HAPPY THAN NOT. It’s just not possible. The characters—especially Aaron—will always stay with me, and that’s okay. It’s okay because I want them to linger inside of my mind. It’s okay because they deserve to.<br><br><b>
  <b>
    <i>Sometimes pain is so unmanageable that the idea of spending another day with it seems impossible. Other times pain acts as a compass to help you get through the messier tunnels of growing up. But the pain can help you find happiness if you can remember it.</i>
  </b>
</b><br><br>________________________________________<br><br><b>I have to read this book.</b> Here's why:<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1428262766i/14397398._SX540_.jpg" width="400" height="284" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>If you don't know the lovely <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/7579036.Becky_Albertalli" title="Becky Albertalli" rel="nofollow noopener">Becky Albertalli</a>, she's the author of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/19547856.Simon_vs__the_Homo_Sapiens_Agenda__Creekwood___1_" title="Simon vs. the Homo Sapiens Agenda (Creekwood, #1) by Becky Albertalli" rel="nofollow noopener">Simon vs. the Homo Sapiens Agenda</a>. ❤</span>

<div id="review_1054339198" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1054339198" />
    <a title="Emily May" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4622890-emily-may"><img alt="Emily May" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1528390751p2/4622890.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1054339198?book_show_action=true">Sep 13, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Emily May" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Emily May" href="/user/show/4622890-emily-may">Emily May</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=arc">arc</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=2015">2015</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1054339198" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2099352399784664377"><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>“This is still an ugly world.”</b>
  </i>
</blockquote><br/>I opened with that quote for a reason - while definitely entertaining, <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/19542841.More_Happy_Than_Not' title='More Happy Than Not by Adam Silvera' rel='nofollow noopener'>More Happy Than Not</a> is a dark, sad book that deals with homophobia, depression and suicide. The quirky dialogue and nerdy references to comic books, Star Wars and action heroes are much needed to lighten up an otherwise very distressing novel.<br/><br/>Personally, I do not think the promised big twist is particularly hard to guess if you've read the description and <a class='jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction'>(view spoiler)</a><span class='spoilerContainer' style='display: none'>[seen the movie</span></span>
  <span id="freeText2099352399784664377" style="display:none"><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>“This is still an ugly world.”</b>
  </i>
</blockquote><br />I opened with that quote for a reason - while definitely entertaining, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/19542841.More_Happy_Than_Not" title="More Happy Than Not by Adam Silvera" rel="nofollow noopener">More Happy Than Not</a> is a dark, sad book that deals with homophobia, depression and suicide. The quirky dialogue and nerdy references to comic books, Star Wars and action heroes are much needed to lighten up an otherwise very distressing novel.<br /><br />Personally, I do not think the promised big twist is particularly hard to guess if you've read the description and <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[seen the movie this is being compared to <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>, but I don't think much hangs on it anyway. Because this book is <b>an overlapping of several stories and themes</b>, each one as powerful as the last. It's about coming to terms with ones sexuality, it's about friendship, it's about memory and forgetting, it's a love story, and it's about choosing to be happy, despite the sad.<br /><br />Oh, and it's also one of the <b>most diverse books I've ever read</b>. And, unlike other books that try to do many things at once, all the many themes are executed well.<br /><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>"From the shapes cast by the green paper lantern, you would never know that there were two boys sitting closely to one another trying to find themselves. You would only see shadows hugging, indiscriminate."</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br />The story is about Aaron, who is trying to pick himself up after both his father's suicide and his own attempted suicide. He can't turn to his family or guy friends, and his girlfriend tries to be supportive but Aaron doesn't really feel able to talk to her either. When sweet, eccentric Thomas comes along, he's everything Aaron needs in his life and more. Suddenly, Aaron has to deal with the realization that he's gay in a place where being gay isn't welcomed, or choose to not deal with it - by going to the Leteo institute and having his memories taken away.<br /><br />Obviously a book about depression, suicide and homophobia would be sad, but I think it's the other little things that make <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/19542841.More_Happy_Than_Not" title="More Happy Than Not by Adam Silvera" rel="nofollow noopener">More Happy Than Not</a> an emotional read. Like the suggestion running behind every event in the book that sometimes life doesn't turn out the way you wanted it to and you don't always get what you longed for, and the message that wiping it all away (either through suicide or memory loss) isn't the answer. And the fact that wiping away memories doesn't change who you are. <br /><br /><b>And the love story</b>. Don't be fooled into thinking this is another cute teen romance, though it definitely is cute at times. It's built up gradually through friendship, geekery and mutual understanding, until it's something else...<br /><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“He rubs his face and his eyes squint; a tear escapes. “You didn’t have to take my side, Stretch.” I kind of, sort of, definitely always will.</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br />I'm serious, though, this isn't a nice book. You've been warned. The teens might have cute moments, but they're also real teens who masturbate, watch porn and curse (though there's not a lot of profanity if that bothers you). And ALL the characters are well-developed, confused and often funny.<br /><br />In short, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/19542841.More_Happy_Than_Not" title="More Happy Than Not by Adam Silvera" rel="nofollow noopener">More Happy Than Not</a> is a blend of light and dark, happiness and not-happiness, and it's incredibly effective. If I were cheesy I'd call it <i>unforgettable</i>. Ah well, it's nearly Friday so... it's unforgettable. Go read it.<br /><br /><a href="http://thebookgeek.co.uk" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> | <a href="https://www.facebook.com/thebookgeekreviews" rel="nofollow noopener">Facebook</a> | <a href="https://twitter.com/thebookgeek01" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> | <a href="http://instagram.com/emleemay" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a> | <a href="http://mycountryheart.co.uk/" rel="nofollow noopener">Tumblr</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="2099352399784664377" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <a title="jessica" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/10171516-jessica"><img alt="jessica" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1509983330p2/10171516.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2381255140?book_show_action=true">May 04, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="jessica" class="user" itemprop="url" name="jessica" href="/user/show/10171516-jessica">jessica</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2381255140" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13829326734674543647">i seem to have found myself unintentionally reading silveras bibliography in reverse chronological order and his books just keep getting sadder and sadder. but there is something in that sadness he creates. something living. something real. its something that makes you realise that heartbreak is good because it means youre alive. and you begin to learn that positives can come from the negatives, that pain doesnt have to be the end. you grow and understand and become the person you want to be. an</span>
  <span id="freeText13829326734674543647" style="display:none">i seem to have found myself unintentionally reading silveras bibliography in reverse chronological order and his books just keep getting sadder and sadder. but there is something in that sadness he creates. something living. something real. its something that makes you realise that heartbreak is good because it means youre alive. and you begin to learn that positives can come from the negatives, that pain doesnt have to be the end. you grow and understand and become the person you want to be. and then suddenly, you realise youre more happy than not.<br /><br /><b>↠ <i>4 stars</i></b></span>

<div id="review_796471279" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

Aaron's voice is pitch-perfect, and it's impossible to read this book without falling in love with him.<br/>2. It is full of surprises and twists and emotional highs and lows, to the point where putting the book down is almost physically painful.<br/>3. It will break your heart in the best possible way.<br/><br/>Beautiful, beautiful book.</span>

<div id="review_1296714862" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1296714862" />
    <a title="Thomas" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2018505-thomas"><img alt="Thomas" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1567953607p2/2018505.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1296714862?book_show_action=true">Jun 02, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Thomas" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Thomas" href="/user/show/2018505-thomas">Thomas</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2018505-thomas?shelf=2nd-favorites">2nd-favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2018505-thomas?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2018505-thomas?shelf=five-stars">five-stars</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2018505-thomas?shelf=lgbtq">lgbtq</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2018505-thomas?shelf=realistic-fiction">realistic-fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1296714862" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16090269501515616394">Reading <i>More Happy Than Not</i> and witnessing the SCOTUS decision on gay marriage has made me a super emotional wreck this week, in the best way possible. This book may even tie <i>Aristotle and Dante Discover the Secrets of the Universe</i> for my favorite YA book, and if anyone here has read <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/12000020-aristotle-and-dante-discover-the-secrets-of-the-universe?ac=1' rel='nofollow noopener'>my review</a> of Saenz's story, you know that means high praise. So, without further ado, I give you:<br/><br/><b>Five Reasons Why <i>More Happy Than Not</i> has Renewed My Faith in YA Fiction:</b><br/><br/>1) <b>This book is so freaking sad.</b> Forget plots </span>
  <span id="freeText16090269501515616394" style="display:none">Reading <i>More Happy Than Not</i> and witnessing the SCOTUS decision on gay marriage has made me a super emotional wreck this week, in the best way possible. This book may even tie <i>Aristotle and Dante Discover the Secrets of the Universe</i> for my favorite YA book, and if anyone here has read <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/12000020-aristotle-and-dante-discover-the-secrets-of-the-universe?ac=1" rel="nofollow noopener">my review</a> of Saenz's story, you know that means high praise. So, without further ado, I give you:<br /><br /><b>Five Reasons Why <i>More Happy Than Not</i> has Renewed My Faith in YA Fiction:</b><br /><br />1) <b>This book is so freaking sad.</b> Forget plots about an uninterested love interest or an absent parent or a group of vampires gone awry. <i>More Happy Than Not</i> transcends the typical YA story by incorporating themes of loss and self-regret in mature, oftentimes open-ended ways. Yes, Adam Silvera ties in comic books, video games, and other normal aspects of adolescent life into the book. However, he still manages to capture and reflect the convoluted suffering so many teens go through on a day-to-day basis because of factors like their sexuality. I 100% wish that this book had been there for me when I struggled with my gayness as a middle school student, and I feel so glad knowing that it is available to young folk now.<br /><br />2) <b>This book deals with sexuality in a complex and multifaceted way.</b> Some say writers should stop writing coming out stories. Others say that we will always need coming out stories. I say that we should find an in between, that we should take contemporary society into account and create books that exemplify our progress while still honoring those in less fortunate families and/or situations. <i>More Happy Than Not</i> does just that, because though it may look like a coming out story at first glance, it compounds and deepens Aaron's journey: though his sexuality may play a huge part in the book, it only really scratches the surface of Aaron's character and his experiences, a fabulous move by Silvera. A short quote that portrays just an ounce of the rawness within this novel:<br /><br /><i>"I'm the liar, not him. I lied to Genevieve, to my friends, to everyone. But I've pushed my limit and here's the truth: this is the most painfully confusing time in life and he's the first person who said all the right words to me and reminds me of the first days of summer where you leave home without jacket, and my favorite songs playing over and over. And now he may never talk to me again."</i><br /><br />3) <b>This book is just super diverse in general.</b> It weaves in memory loss and retrieval, race, both accepting and non-accepting friends and family, a girlfriend, class, and a sort-of-maybe boyfriend, and more. Unlike other authors, Silvera writes these themes and motifs into his story in a way that radiates authenticity and emotion; it never feels like he throws them in just for the sake of throwing them in. Each disparate part of the plot adds onto other elements of the plot, creating a thorough and seamless book that reads without a hitch.<br /><br />4) <b>This book's characters are basically perfect.</b> They are perfect because of their splendid imperfections. Silvera imbues every individual in this book with a sense of reality: not only are they diverse in race, gender, age, and occupation, but they also vary in their likability and the mistakes they make. All of these characters - Thomas, Aaron's closest friend, Aaron's mother, who cares about Aaron with all of her heart, even Aaron himself - have internal and external struggles they must deal with, and each of them do so in messy, honest ways. While it would have been easy to construct a single antagonist for the entire story, Silvera sticks to creating complicated and substantial characters, people you will find yourself thinking about long after finish the novel.<br /><br />5) <b>This book is hopeful.</b> Despite the layers of sadness and despair rooted in <i>More Happy Than Not</i>, Silvera makes sure to blend in messages of redemption, joy, and bittersweet acceptance throughout the story. Aaron's happiness does not come easy; it is the product of physical and mental pain, heartbreak, and great loss. However, Silvera shows the complexity of life, how its most aching moments may lead to its most serene satisfactions, and how in the end we all must maintain a never-ending hope, both for ourselves and for others. This book highlights one of the main reasons I read young-adult fiction: to empathize with the deep emotions that come from great adversity and to remind myself that our worst suffering often brings our brightest light. Silvera shows us that light, its fragile beauty and its gentle strength. One last small quote, from one of my favorite scenes in the story:<br /><br /><i>"But for tonight, this is enough. From the shapes cast by the green paper lantern, you would never know that were were two boys sitting closely to one another trying to find themselves. You would only see shadows hugging, indiscriminate."</i> <br /><br />If Silvera's debut novel acts as any indication, he has a long and successful writing career ahead of him. If he continues to produce, I can already see "Silvera" as a trademark in YA, similar to "Dessen" or "Sanchez" or "Stiefvater." I cannot wait to read <i>History Is All You Left Me</i> in 2016. I cannot wait to see what other people think of this book.</span>
  <a data-text-id="16090269501515616394" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1304989260" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1304989260" />
    <a title="Kai" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/41788524-kai"><img alt="Kai" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1573562141p2/41788524.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1304989260?book_show_action=true">Jun 11, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kai" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kai" href="/user/show/41788524-kai">Kai</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/41788524-kai?shelf=owned">owned</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/41788524-kai?shelf=2015">2015</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/41788524-kai?shelf=queer">queer</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1304989260" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8339880053841767620"><i>“The boy with no direction taught me something unforgettable: happiness comes again if you let it.”</i><br/><br/>I've waited so so long (well, since this was released I guess) to read this. This was one of my most anticipated books of 2015 and it did not let me down.<br/>Adam Silvera seems to be a cool guy. I like the way he interacts with social media, I think he's quite funny and so is his writing style. Maybe not his novel(because yeah it is kind of sad) but definitely his writing style.<br/><br/>This was a page-turner f</span>
  <span id="freeText8339880053841767620" style="display:none"><i>“The boy with no direction taught me something unforgettable: happiness comes again if you let it.”</i><br /><br />I've waited so so long (well, since this was released I guess) to read this. This was one of my most anticipated books of 2015 and it did not let me down.<br />Adam Silvera seems to be a cool guy. I like the way he interacts with social media, I think he's quite funny and so is his writing style. Maybe not his novel(because yeah it is kind of sad) but definitely his writing style.<br /><br />This was a page-turner from start to finish. I really got a feeling for the protagonist's surroundings, his family and friends. And I don't know why but I pictured Aaron as Adam all the time...I mean even the names are quite alike. And the tallness. And the gayness. And the living-in-the-Bronxness.<br />And I guess while this could have just been a wonderful bittersweet, kind of tragic YA love story, the science-fiction in there added an utterly intriguing and devastating edge to it. <br /><i> More Happy Than Not </i> took me by surprise, big time. Not only once (Part Zero) but twice (No More Tomorrows).<br /><br />The only thing that bugged me, is that I could not get lost in it. While I felt for Aaron, I did not feel with Aaron. That would have made it a 5-star rating.<br /><br /><a href="https://www.instagram.com/fantasticbooksandwheretofindem/" rel="nofollow noopener">Find more of my books on Instagram</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="8339880053841767620" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1579880529" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1579880529" />
    <a title="Brian Yahn" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/22849115-brian-yahn"><img alt="Brian Yahn" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1464719293p2/22849115.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1579880529?book_show_action=true">Mar 14, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Brian Yahn" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Brian Yahn" href="/user/show/22849115-brian-yahn">Brian Yahn</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1579880529" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8367657169158769198">Adam Silvera's writing immediately absorbed me into the life of Aaron Soto--a troubled youth anxious to lose his virginity. And making the obvious comparison of the Leteo Institute's memory procedure to <i>Eternal Sunshine of the Spotless Mind</i>, I was definitely intrigued to see where the story would go, especially since I was enjoying the prose so much. The realness of it swept me away like <i>The Catcher in the Rye</i>. There was something kind of immature about how giddy I was to read about this fictiti</span>
  <span id="freeText8367657169158769198" style="display:none">Adam Silvera's writing immediately absorbed me into the life of Aaron Soto--a troubled youth anxious to lose his virginity. And making the obvious comparison of the Leteo Institute's memory procedure to <i>Eternal Sunshine of the Spotless Mind</i>, I was definitely intrigued to see where the story would go, especially since I was enjoying the prose so much. The realness of it swept me away like <i>The Catcher in the Rye</i>. There was something kind of immature about how giddy I was to read about this fictitious kid, angsty to lose his virginity, but alas, I was turning pages and giggly like an idiot, and shamelessly loving every second of it.<br /><br />Predictably, this isn't just a story about a kid getting laid. No, it quickly moves into a new direction, into what seems to be a new instalove relationship, and the way it does is cliched enough to almost ruin that awesome sense of realness earlier established. It doesn't quite reach that level, though, and the relationship evolves into a plot-based romance thriller, which completely explains that early awkward stage, making it more than excusable, making it justified. The realness seeps back into the story through twists and turns and revelations of dark character secrets that propel the story in a page-turning fashion right up to the end, a finish that unfortunately didn't satisfy me. It seems to paint being gay in a toxically unhealthy and hopeless way. That combined with all the suicidal stuff, it just really rubbed me the wrong way.<br /><br />I used to think this instalove relationship between Aaron and Thomas was pretty ridiculous. I thought I'd been in love a couple of times in my life, but after meeting someone new, I'm questioning if I ever have been. What I once thought to be laughably absurd -- two people being completely heals over head in love in three weeks -- now seems kind of accurate, especially for teenagers.<br /><br /><i>More Happy Than Not</i> is unquestionably more good than not.</span>
  <a data-text-id="8367657169158769198" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1981886693" />

        rated it

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14002983-charlotte-may?shelf=tear-jerker">tear-jerker</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1981886693" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10529631091154946689">😭😭😭😭 I’m ok. I think I might be broken. But I’m ok. <br/><br/>This book broke me into a million pieces. Adam Silvera needs to start sending out wavers for people to sign before reading his books, because good God I am damaged!<br/><br/>First was <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/35216509.They_Both_Die_at_the_End' title='They Both Die at the End by Adam Silvera' rel='nofollow noopener'>They Both Die at the End</a>(we ALL knew how that would go down) but with the title of this one, I hoped for slightly less heartbreak and soul crushing. BUT I was wrong. So wrong.<br/><br/>The blurb doesn’t give much to go on. Aaron has been dating Genevieve for 1 year, and they’ve been </span>
  <span id="freeText10529631091154946689" style="display:none">😭😭😭😭 I’m ok. I think I might be broken. But I’m ok. <br /><br />This book broke me into a million pieces. Adam Silvera needs to start sending out wavers for people to sign before reading his books, because good God I am damaged!<br /><br />First was <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/35216509.They_Both_Die_at_the_End" title="They Both Die at the End by Adam Silvera" rel="nofollow noopener">They Both Die at the End</a>(we ALL knew how that would go down) but with the title of this one, I hoped for slightly less heartbreak and soul crushing. BUT I was wrong. So wrong.<br /><br />The blurb doesn’t give much to go on. Aaron has been dating Genevieve for 1 year, and they’ve been through A LOT. Between Aaron’s fathers’ suicide and Aaron’s own suicide attempt, it’s safe to say that his emotions are rocky. But he and Genevieve have always been stable, and she has always brought him through to the other side. But when new guy Thomas shows up, Aaron and he hit it off right away, soon they are spending loads of time together, much to the dismay of Aaron’s other friends from the projects.<br /><br />Looming in the background is the Leteo Procedure. A medical procedure that can infiltrate the human brain and remove certain memories, designed to make people forget horrible things in their pasts. However wonderful this procedure seems to the masses, it comes with risks; the main one being that your memories are in danger of being <i>unwound</i> if you come into contact with something related to what you have forgotten. Be it a person, a scent, a place or an event. It’s very Eternal Sunshine of the Spotless Mind – which was right up my alley.<br /><br />Without giving anything away, later in the book Aaron decides he wants a Leteo procedure, and is determined to get one, whatever it takes. The twist provided in the book I thought was very good, <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ Aaron is beaten up after being seen hugging Thomas. His ‘friends’ are massive homophobes and they nearly kill him. This act of violence causes Thomas’ memories to unwind – meaning he has actually had the Leteo procedure in the past, but can’t remember it (obviously). He unwinds to memories of another relationship – with a boy called Collin; of being punched the shit out of by his dad when he comes out to him; of Collin breaking things off with him, and finally with Aaron’s dad committing suicide, for which Aaron blames himself.  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />There are so many emotions in this book, fear, anger, sadness but there is also hope. This book is an absolute whirlwind and I now hold Adam Silvera personally responsible for my broken heart.</span>
  <a data-text-id="10529631091154946689" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  <span id="freeText903769403848865173" style="display:none"><b>you won't admit you love me.</b><br><br> <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1458430723ra/18488295.gif" width="400" height="400" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>this will not be a useful review of this book, and i'm sorry.<br><br>i just... never did figure out how to sort out my feelings another way.<br><br>__________<br><br><br>i need a minute<br>need a minute and a minute and a minute more<br>heart pounds and my throat's so tight<br>memories aren't my friends tonight<br><br>__________<br><br><br>falling in love for the first time was like sliding down a bannister. <br><br>maybe you know what i mean. <br><br>a bannister like the ones you see in a public school. long, and in the middle of the stairs, terminating above a concrete landing covered over by ghastly green linoleum buffed to a dull shine. <br><br>maybe you've never done it before, this badass slide down a thirty foot rail at a forty-five degree angle, and maybe you think it's probably a bad idea—but you've seen other kids do it, and it looks awesome.<br><br>if only you could ever get up the courage.<br><br>maybe you lean your hip against it, a couple different times, talking to a friend, pretending not to be standing there on the stairs wondering what it might be like to hurtle down to a spectacularly lithe and athletic landing you'll pretend isn't actually the coolest thing you've ever done, ever.<br><br>and maybe, <i>maaaybe</i> one time you're there long after the last class has let out for the day, and you know you're going to do it right then, when the building is empty of anyone you'd want to see you triumph, as well as everyone you wouldn't want to see you fall.<br><br>so you hypothetically do the thing, maybe. <br><br>perhaps you sit your ass on it, and at once realize that's maybe not quite right, so you scoot back a bit so your weight's resting mostly on your thighs. <br><br>and you sorta... sorta slide a bit. just a little. <br><br>maybe you panic and clutch at the pitted metal bar to stop yourself, and then feel silly when you realize you've only moved two steps down.<br><br>maybe now's when you tell yourself: i can do this.<br><br>and then maybe you do.<br><br>maybe you let go, and for the first few seconds of glorious acceleration you're thinking this is the best thing ever, and what you wouldn't give to have that asshole c*****—not martinez, or prieto, or gonzales, or de silva—the other one—<br><br>—the one for whom you've maybe hidden a love in the most secret and tender deeps of your heart since the third fucking grade.<br><br>yeah, <i>that</i> c*****.<br><br>what you wouldn't give to see him standing at the bottom with a smile on his face, watching you be awesome.<br><br>but maybe he's not there, just then.<br><br>maybe he heard you came out of the closet a month ago, all angry and belligerent during a heated disagreement in black history class. <br><br>maybe this abrupt failure in homo tradecraft happened to result in a fistfight, a desk thrown clear across a classroom, and a chip in your front tooth—and maybe now he doesn't wanna talk to you anymore.<br><br>maybe junior high has started feeling like one long ending instead of the glorious beginning you and him used to imagine.<br><br>or maybe it's just the usual hollow feeling you live with, passing him in the halls and pretending like you don't see the stony indifference in his face as he walks by, still, always, all this time after he ditched you. <br><br>whatever it is, maybe it withers your joy, a third of the way down this theoretical bannister, when it occurs to you that you are at terminal velocity and to put a foot down to stop just this second would mean busting your ass all the way down a flight of stairs and maybe dying un-lithely and un-athletically and holy balls you <i>knew</i> you should have worn literally anything other than your star wars boxers today bcuz hello, autopsies.<br><br>but maybe you don't die. <br><br>maybe you stick the landing like motherfucking dominique dawes at the atlanta olympic games.<br><br>and maybe, maybe it’s not so sharp, this time, the ache you feel as you slowly lower the arms you’ve thrown up in silent exultation, because you realize the feel of all that empty air around your body is maybe not so bad, kinda, compared to the feel of the arm he might have casually wound around your neck to celebrate.<br><br>so maybe you go home.<br><br>maybe you shove your hypothetical headphones into your hypothetical ears and listen to your favorite hypothetical cassette on the hypothetical bus ride to your hypothetical home.<br><br>maybe music is the only way you even have a shot at going a single hour without thinking about the friend who used to sit in the seat next to you.<br><br>maybe you know this. and turn the volume up.<br><br>and maybe everything’s just fine.<br><br><br></span>

    <a title="karen" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/45618-karen"><img alt="karen" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1596291582p2/45618.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1204809290?book_show_action=true">Feb 20, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="karen" class="user" itemprop="url" name="karen" href="/user/show/45618-karen">karen</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/45618-karen?shelf=titles-that-lie">titles-that-lie</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/45618-karen?shelf=why-yes-i-ya">why-yes-i-ya</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/45618-karen?shelf=books-that-made-me-cry">books-that-made-me-cry</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1204809290" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13069418499857452740"><b>	fulfilling my 2019 goal to read (at least) one book each month that has been digitally moldering, unread, on my NOOK for years and years and years.</b><br/><br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1550884990i/27105413._SX540_.png' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>one of the benefits of letting a book ripen on your NOOK for years and years and years is that you forget what the book is about and why you wanted to read it in the first place. you just know that february is a short month and you’ve set this NOOK-goal for yourself and as you find yourself getting closer to the end of the month, you panic and decide</span>
  <span id="freeText13069418499857452740" style="display:none"><b>	fulfilling my 2019 goal to read (at least) one book each month that has been digitally moldering, unread, on my NOOK for years and years and years.</b><br><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1550884990i/27105413._SX540_.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>one of the benefits of letting a book ripen on your NOOK for years and years and years is that you forget what the book is about and why you wanted to read it in the first place. you just know that february is a short month and you’ve set this NOOK-goal for yourself and as you find yourself getting closer to the end of the month, you panic and decide to read the first YA book you see because at least you know it will be fast.<br><br>all you really remember is that this is supposed to be sad, and it is immediately clear it's gonna have suicide themes, but you shrug, knowing that books just don't make you cry, ever, and your life has been more affected by suicide than many people's, so no damn <i>book</i> is gonna push you over the edge into weepytown because that earth is scorched, son. and you were right. none of the suicide stuff comes close to making you cry. <br><br>but that one page, towards the end? yeah, that broke through your defenses, causing some sustained eyeleak on the 7 train. and you loved feeling like an empathic reader for once. <br><br>this book's a few years old, and there are some hints to the book's tricks in the comparisons made by other reviews and the book's own synopsis. but some of us didn't bother to (re)read any of those before diving into this book, and weeeeeee were completely caught off-guard once that blindfold was lifted. and it was awesome. <br><br>to switch pronouns ONE MORE TIME, that turn happened while i was crossing the street, reading this, and i fullstopped directly in the middle of queens boulevard and said "ohhhhhhhhhhhh DAMN!" <br><br>that complete "didn't see it coming" shock is as delightful to me as a book that makes me cry, although it is much less rare. i'm not sure there has been a book, before now, that has done both to me. no spoilers from me, just genuine pleasure at what i thought was gonna be a throwaway read just to meet my goals and instead turned out to be a magnificent heartpunching story. <br><br>this book is the chinese water torture* of sad and eventually, it will break you down. <br><br>and you will love it.<br><br><br><br>*unless that's one of those things we don't say anymore? in which case, replace with some imaginary game called "sad, sadder, saddest." <br><br>*************************************<br><br>yes, friends, there were tears. even a shriveled old heart like mine can still sometimes feel.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1483664768ra/21637120.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>review to come.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1528725630i/25720315.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><a href="http://bloggycomelately.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">come to my blog!</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="13069418499857452740" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<span id="freeTextContainer1504528291993292685">3.5 stars<br/><br/>I have mixed feelings. The downfall is that I really really really wanted to like this book, but I'm just not a huge fan of books that require the suspension of disbelief, mostly in books like this contemporary/sci-fi hybrid. The whole sci-fi aspect was really thought-provoking, but I don't think it was developed well enough to be impactful as an element in the story. So even though the majority of the book is rooted in reality, there was just enough of that weird twist to make it feel </span>
  <span id="freeText1504528291993292685" style="display:none">3.5 stars<br /><br />I have mixed feelings. The downfall is that I really really really wanted to like this book, but I'm just not a huge fan of books that require the suspension of disbelief, mostly in books like this contemporary/sci-fi hybrid. The whole sci-fi aspect was really thought-provoking, but I don't think it was developed well enough to be impactful as an element in the story. So even though the majority of the book is rooted in reality, there was just enough of that weird twist to make it feel too much at arm's length. <br /><br />But I did like the characters. Aaron had an interesting mind to delve into. Gen wasn't two-demensional like one might expect a side character like her to be. I loved Thomas. I loved (?) Collin. <br /><br />I guess the ending of this book just made me conflicted. Silvera discussed the "not every story has a happy ending" but this just felt like it threw me into a river then left me to fend for myself?? I don't really understand the plot twist that led us there, and all of the characters in the end just sorta.... go away. It was strange and left me wanting more, especially since we discovered the depth of Aaron's history, and I wanted him to be able to make peace with it more tangibly. Oh well.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer9387048202442061849">A few days ago my good friend, and talented author, Adam Silvera posted this piece on his blog: Happiness Isn’t Just an Outside Thing. The blog post talks mainly about depression, which Adam has grappled with for some time now, and is a beautiful meditation on the failure of external validation to satisfy the holes that truly need filling. I’m so proud of him for sharing his hard journey with all his readers with the same incisive honesty that makes him such a fantastic writer.<br/><br/>On that note, a fe</span>
  <span id="freeText9387048202442061849" style="display:none">A few days ago my good friend, and talented author, Adam Silvera posted this piece on his blog: Happiness Isn’t Just an Outside Thing. The blog post talks mainly about depression, which Adam has grappled with for some time now, and is a beautiful meditation on the failure of external validation to satisfy the holes that truly need filling. I’m so proud of him for sharing his hard journey with all his readers with the same incisive honesty that makes him such a fantastic writer.<br /><br />On that note, a few words about his beautiful book, More Happy Than Not,which tells the story of Aaron Soto, a high school student in the Bronx recovering from a recent suicide attempt. Aaron has a lot of reasons to feel sad. His father’s suicide, his overworked mother, and his confusing feelings for the new guy on the block. Aaron starts to wonder if the Leteo Institute, which promises revolutionary mind-alterations, might be a good solution to all his problems. <br /><br />With courage, clarity, and a unique voice, More Happy Than Not, is a must read for everyone.</span>
  <a data-text-id="9387048202442061849" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1314755669" />
    <a title="Kelly (and the Book Boar)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/11183856-kelly-and-the-book-boar"><img alt="Kelly (and the Book Boar)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1530646317p2/11183856.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1314755669?book_show_action=true">Jun 22, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kelly (and the Book Boar)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kelly (and the Book Boar)" href="/user/show/11183856-kelly-and-the-book-boar">Kelly (and the Book Boar)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11183856-kelly-and-the-book-boar?shelf=liburrrrrry-book">liburrrrrry-book</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11183856-kelly-and-the-book-boar?shelf=lgbtq">lgbtq</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11183856-kelly-and-the-book-boar?shelf=read-in-2015">read-in-2015</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11183856-kelly-and-the-book-boar?shelf=ya-for-grown-ups">ya-for-grown-ups</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11183856-kelly-and-the-book-boar?shelf=like-this-or-we-cant-be-friends">like-this-or-we-cant-be-friends</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1314755669" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5980132833592640219">Find all of my reviews at: <a target='_blank' rel='noopener nofollow' href='http://52bookminimum.blogspot.com/'>http://52bookminimum.blogspot.com/</a><br/><br/><b>
  <i>"It's okay how some stories leave off without an ending. Life doesn't always deliver the one you would expect."</i>
</b><br/><br/>Holy book slump, Batman! I was on a tear through 2 and 3 Star books when <i>More Happy Than Not</i> finally queued up at the library. Then <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1181272997?book_show_action=false&from_review_page=1' rel='nofollow noopener'>Larry</a> told me I had to love it or we could no longer be friends, but I had to go watch my kids lose 427 baseball games first so I left the book on the table . . . <br/><br/><a href='http://www.freeimagehosting.net/commercial-photography/texas/houston/' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1437144546ra/15542404.gif' alt='Houston commercial photography' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><br/><br/>When I finally returned (</span>
  <span id="freeText5980132833592640219" style="display:none">Find all of my reviews at: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://52bookminimum.blogspot.com/">http://52bookminimum.blogspot.com/</a><br><br><b>
  <i>"It's okay how some stories leave off without an ending. Life doesn't always deliver the one you would expect."</i>
</b><br><br>Holy book slump, Batman! I was on a tear through 2 and 3 Star books when <i>More Happy Than Not</i> finally queued up at the library. Then <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1181272997?book_show_action=false&amp;from_review_page=1" rel="nofollow noopener">Larry</a> told me I had to love it or we could no longer be friends, but I had to go watch my kids lose 427 baseball games first so I left the book on the table . . . <br><br><a href="http://www.freeimagehosting.net/commercial-photography/texas/houston/" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1437144546ra/15542404.gif" alt="Houston commercial photography" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>When I finally returned (my albino skin red as a beet from all of the outdoorsiness), I threw some meat products on the table for my family's dinner and informed them they were to leave me be. And I <b>devoured</b> this book. What is the limit of how much I loved this story????<br><br><a href="http://www.freeimagehosting.net/commercial-photography/texas/houston/" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1437144546ra/15542405.gif" alt="Houston commercial photography" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>That's right, Blowhan. The limit does not exist. <br><br>I'm not going to tell you a whole lot about <i>More Happy Than Not</i>. Basically, this is the story of 16-year old Aaron - a boy whose father committed suicide a few months ago and now lives in the projects with his family. It's about choosing a different path for himself . . . <br><br><b>
  <i>"I can't believe I was once that guy who carved a smile into his wrist because he couldn't find happiness, that guy who thought he would find it in death."</i>
</b><br><br>It's about Aaron's day-to-day life hanging with his friends and girlfriend, and about the new kid, Thomas, who quickly becomes his best friend and who makes everything about Aaron's world kind of go topsy-turvy . . . . <br><br><b>
  <i>"From the shapes cast by the green paper lantern, you would never know that there were two boys sitting closely to one another trying to find themselves. You would only see shadows hugging indiscriminate."</i>
</b><br><br>It's about memories . . . <br><br><b>
  <i>"Some can be sucker punching, others carry you forward, some stay with you forever, others you forget on your own."</i>
</b><br><br>And about dealing with pain . . . <br><br><b>
  <i>"Sometimes pain is so unmanageable that the idea of spending another day with it seems impossible. Other times pain acts as a compass to help you get through the messier tunnels of growing up. But the pain can only help you find happiness if you can remember it."</i>
</b><br><br>Most of all, it's a completely unique take on coming of age that almost made me have some feelings . . . <br><br><a href="http://www.freeimagehosting.net/commercial-photography/texas/houston/" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1437144546ra/15542406.gif" alt="Houston commercial photography" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>But I'm not a baby so I kept my s&amp;^t together.<br><br>This ain't your typical Young Adult selection, friends. Adam Silvera's approach is 100% original and it totally blew me away. It gets every star and I can't wait to see what he comes up with next.</span>
  <a data-text-id="5980132833592640219" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>


      <div class="reviewFooter uitext buttons">

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_1288693299" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1288693299" />
    <a title="Alienor ✘ French Frowner ✘" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/31461418-alienor-french-frowner"><img alt="Alienor ✘ French Frowner ✘" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1532688964p2/31461418.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1288693299?book_show_action=true">May 24, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Alienor ✘ French Frowner ✘" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Alienor ✘ French Frowner ✘" href="/user/show/31461418-alienor-french-frowner">Alienor ✘ French Frowner ✘</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31461418-alienor-french-frowner?shelf=knots-in-my-stomach">knots-in-my-stomach</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31461418-alienor-french-frowner?shelf=scifi">scifi</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31461418-alienor-french-frowner?shelf=lgbtqia">lgbtqia</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31461418-alienor-french-frowner?shelf=likeable-mc">likeable-mc</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31461418-alienor-french-frowner?shelf=fave-ya-and-fantasy">fave-ya-and-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31461418-alienor-french-frowner?shelf=2015-read">2015-read</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31461418-alienor-french-frowner?shelf=made-me-laugh">made-me-laugh</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31461418-alienor-french-frowner?shelf=all-time-favorites">all-time-favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31461418-alienor-french-frowner?shelf=fave-2015-contenders">fave-2015-contenders</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31461418-alienor-french-frowner?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1288693299" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16510850878909337333"><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1434666463i/15251005._SX540_.png' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><i>Oh, boy. <b>I won't</b></i>.<br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1434666463i/15251006._SX540_.png' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><i>More Happy Than Not</i> didn't turn out to be what I expected, and let me tell you, it was so much better than I thought it would be. Messed-up when you think about it, this containing <s>one of my biggest pet peeve</s> <i>make it plural</i> : several of my biggest pet peeves - nah, I won't tell which ones, I can be annoying like that. But let's start at the beginning, shall we? <br/><br/>There are books that make you feel like a <i>voyeur</i>, as the characters seem so real that you get the impression to spy on </span>
  <span id="freeText16510850878909337333" style="display:none"><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1434666463i/15251005._SX540_.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><i>Oh, boy. <b>I won't</b></i>.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1434666463i/15251006._SX540_.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><i>More Happy Than Not</i> didn't turn out to be what I expected, and let me tell you, it was so much better than I thought it would be. Messed-up when you think about it, this containing <s>one of my biggest pet peeve</s> <i>make it plural</i> : several of my biggest pet peeves - nah, I won't tell which ones, I can be annoying like that. But let's start at the beginning, shall we? <br><br>There are books that make you feel like a <i>voyeur</i>, as the characters seem so real that you get the impression to spy on them, somehow. <i>More Happy Than Not</i> definitely belongs to that category, and hooked me from the very first sentence.<br><br><blockquote>
  <b>"Sometimes your story is worth reading about because your life sucks," I say. "And I don't think your life sucks."</b>
</blockquote><br>How can I explain why? It just - <i>spoke</i> to me, because I found the characters weirdly relatable. Weirdly, because although my family always navigated on the artistic side of life (yeah, this is <i>so</i> the nice word for odd, sorry mum, love you) I never lived in such a hard way. Yet I can relate on so many levels that I couldn't help but feel drawn into their stories - to feel <i>involved</i> in every fucking event they live. <br><br>This book is full of big issues - issues you better <i>not</i> drop in a book if you don't intend to HANDLE them (including suicide, depression, and homophobia). Well, the fact is, <b>they all were correctly dealt with, and frankly, I'm, kind of, maybe, for sure in awe of Adam Silvera for that.</b> Not that everything is perfect and gets its HEA, NO. It's not. <b>It's messed-up and weird and flawed - yet it's incredible, because you know what? <u>THAT'S HOW LIFE GOES</u></b>. <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1434668065i/15251265._SX540_.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><blockquote>
  <b>"Memories : some can be sucker punching, others carry you forward; some stay with you forever, others you forget on your own."</b>
</blockquote><br><b>TRIGGER WARNING : Suicide</b><br><br>I know, I KNOW, my personal interludes appear pretty often lately, but I can't help myself when it comes to subjects that have a particular resonance for me and <i>oh, well</i>. Don't read it if you don't care. Anyway. Aaron, the main character, has to deal with the consequences of both his father's suicide and his own suicide attempt and expresses how difficult it is for people he loves to trust him again with his own life. In my opinion Adam Silvera captured perfectly how this kind of decisions can affect friendship and family relationships. The truth is, when I was 16 a person very close to me committed several suicidal attempts, and I'd want to say that I was supportive and understanding, I'd want to say that I understood why and how she could do this, I really want to. But sadly, I can't. Sadly, I didn't understand shit. Sadly, I was fucking pissed, because I love her and I couldn't forgive her to give up on us - yes, because I couldn't deal with <i>the Guilt</i>. This fucking guilt you feel when you realize that people you love and live with can suffer without even you noticing. I couldn't deal with the guilt, so I was pissed, furious, mad, everything but what I should have been. But you know what? That's how people react in real life. They aren't perfect. They don't always understand. It took us <i>years</i> to rebuild our relationship after that - it took <i>me</i> years to stop being a fucking brat and accept what she did. Although I'm not proud of it, that's how it is, and I often have a hard time reading stories where characters try to commit suicide because to me, everything is way more complicated and fucked-up that it's portrayed most of the time. <b>All of that is to say that in my modest opinion, the way the author handled this subject here is realistic and really great.</b><br><br><b>END OF THE PERSONAL INTERLUDE</b><br><br>This book? This book caused the weirdest reaction to me : Indeed the day after starting it, I found myself thinking about Aaron, Thomas, Genevieve... like they were real. Like they were friends of mine. And <i>this</i>? <b>This is the best thing I can say about a book</b>. <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1434666463i/15251008._SX540_.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Truth be told, every one of them is realistic and many of them are unlikeable. Despite the fact that I hated several of them <s>first of all Brendan. Talk about a joke of a friend</s>, of course I LOVED how real and complex they were! To be frank, I can't say that they didn't bring memories of actual people I know or used to know, and this is fantastic. Moreover, the writing is perfect because <b>in addition to giving to Aaron a believable, original and oh so endearing voice, it captured perfectly how confusing teenage can be, how difficult it is to resist peer pressure and speak for yourself</b> and for people you love and admire. To fight for who you are and who you want to be. Growing up often goes hand in hand with fucking up (badly). Well, let's be frank, adulthood too. Now, nothing is set in stone. Stand up and deal with it. <br><br>So, yeah. It was cringe-worthy, crude or even annoying at times, but <u>I wouldn't have changed one sentence</u>. <br><br>Most of all I absolutely adored their interactions - sometimes heartbreaking, often smile-inducing, always realistic - they made me <i>so</i> happy, I can't even. <br><br><blockquote>
  <b>(Later I learn that there's even an abandoned musical in his closet about a robot that time-travels back to the Mesozoic era to study dinosaurs while singing about surviving without technology.)</b>
</blockquote><br><u>To sum up</u> : <br>There is porn. There is swearing. There is weed. There is despair. There is fear. There is love. There are comics and YES, cute geeks. There is sex. There are a lot of random stupid games they play to. There are fucking mistakes and maddening decisions. There is LIFE. <b>This sounds <i>true</i> to me.</b><br><br>In a word, this book was a page-turner for me and guys, GUYS! <b>MY FEELS ALL OVER THE PLACE</b>. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1434666463ra/15251009.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Seriously - some parts punched me in the guts and made me <i>sob</i>, others made me want to hit something, yet I smiled so big I can't even express how much love and attachment I feel for Aaron - despite his flaws, his wanderings through life reached out to my heart. That's all I can say.<br><br>Oh well, I'll say it. He fucking broke my heart.<br><br><blockquote>
  <b>"I don't want you too either. Just remember that I love the hell out of you, okay?"</b>
</blockquote><br><u>PS</u> : <i>More Happy Than Not</i> is shelved as Science-Fiction and you might wonder why I didn't address this subject. Actually, even if there are definitely scifi vibes going on at times, and some unexpected twists (HOLY COW), I mostly read it as a contemporary, because it's where lies its strength in my opinion. But I have to admit that it scares me shitless. Trust me, you'll get what I mean. Anyway, I can see why readers could find it unsettling and weird - Promise you'll keep your mind open, okay? <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1434546074i/15235264._SX540_.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1437141825i/15542036._SX540_.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><i>For more of my reviews, please visit:</i><br><blockquote>
  <a href="https://meetthebookworld.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">
    <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1487851828i/22057164._SX540_.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
  </a>
</blockquote></span>
  <a data-text-id="16510850878909337333" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1337170448" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2281821418856142019">Audiobook:<br/> Other than......some of the characters had strange names: Me Crazy, Baby Freddie, Skinny Dave, Fat Dave, and our main character, Aaron gets the nickname of Stretch....<br/>Plus......<br/>there are a lot of nutty games being played: "Manhunt 1 2 3, Manhunt 1 2 3, Manhunt 1 2 3", ...a shark game, 'don't touch green' game, ... plus handball, bikes, rollerblades, fights and fireworks, and tons of swearing....<br/>Add.....<br/>booze, pot, birthdays, horoscope conversation, come childish dialogue, a crappy dig</span>
  <span id="freeText2281821418856142019" style="display:none">Audiobook:<br /> Other than......some of the characters had strange names: Me Crazy, Baby Freddie, Skinny Dave, Fat Dave, and our main character, Aaron gets the nickname of Stretch....<br />Plus......<br />there are a lot of nutty games being played: "Manhunt 1 2 3, Manhunt 1 2 3, Manhunt 1 2 3", ...a shark game, 'don't touch green' game, ... plus handball, bikes, rollerblades, fights and fireworks, and tons of swearing....<br />Add.....<br />booze, pot, birthdays, horoscope conversation, come childish dialogue, a crappy dig about a tattoo parlor ( which I didn't appreciate since I have a daughter who is a tattoo artist), ......<br />THIS BOOK IS KINDA BRILLIANT......<br />And.......<br />Be prepared to have the rug swept from under you!!! In a very thought-provoking way!<br /><br />It's original! Heartbreaking &amp; Heartwarming! Often very funny -often gut-wrenching sad.<br />It's a powerful story dealing with serious complex life issues- with three very likable characters: Aaron, Genevieve, and Thomas! <br /><br />Themes include - and not excluding others....life, love, family, loss, death, depression, friendships, social issues, class, ethnicity, peer pressure, teenage angst, sex, and suicide. <br /><br />Oh yeah.... and this is a YA book -for adults too - contemporary sci-fi.....( do not let the science fiction keep you away from this book). <br /><br /> "Life doesn't always deliver the one you'd expect"<br /><br /><br /><br /></span>

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1301769888" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17504885082794775383">I don't know what to think about this book. I just know it broke me. And that it is definitely NOT more happy than not. It is more like "More depressing than not". Ugh, I ended up so distraught :(.<br/><br/>I kind of liked it, but I could never really connect with the characters, although I really liked a bunch of them (Aaron, Gen, Aaron's mom, Eric, Evangeline and Thomas, specially Thomas). I didn't care about them as much as I feel I should, and I was surprised when I started crying towards the end! So </span>
  <span id="freeText17504885082794775383" style="display:none">I don't know what to think about this book. I just know it broke me. And that it is definitely NOT more happy than not. It is more like "More depressing than not". Ugh, I ended up so distraught :(.<br /><br />I kind of liked it, but I could never really connect with the characters, although I really liked a bunch of them (Aaron, Gen, Aaron's mom, Eric, Evangeline and Thomas, specially Thomas). I didn't care about them as much as I feel I should, and I was surprised when I started crying towards the end! So I warn you: THIS BOOK WILL WRECK YOU. It's a sad, sad book with little glints of happiness. And I have nothing against sad or tragic books, I love them! It's just that this one didn't really do it for me, but it isn't a book I wouldn't recommend.<br /><br />ALSO, I LOVED the plot twist! I wasn't expecting it and it blew my mind, had me reading until 4 AM and I had to work the next day!<br /><br />OH... and before I end this review I just want to said that I HATED Aaron's "friends". UGH, they were just horrible to him all the time and what they did was unforgivable. I wanted to kick them all. They were a gang of stupid and homophobic teenagers!<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="17504885082794775383" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>
